тАШрдЕрдмреБрдзреНрд░рдореН ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдЪрддреБрд░реНрджрд╢рд░реНрдЪрдВ рд╖рд╖реНрдардВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рдзрдирд╛рдХрдкреБрддреНрд░рд╕реНрдп рд▓реБрд╢рд╕реНрдпрд╛рд░реНрд╖рдореН ред рдЗрджрдореБрддреНрддрд░рдВ рдЪ рд╡реИрд╢реНрд╡рджреЗрд╡рдореН ред рддреНрд░рдпреЛрджрд╢реАрдЪрддреБрд░реНрджрд╢реНрдпреМ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрднреМ рд╢рд┐рд╖реНрдЯрд╛ рджреНрд╡рд╛рджрд╢ рдЬрдЧрддреНрдпрдГ ред рддрдерд╛ рдЪрд╛рдиреБрдХреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддрдореН – рдЕрдмреБрдзреНрд░рдВ рд▓реБрд╢реЛ рдзрд╛рдирд╛рдХреЛ рд╡реИрд╢реНрд╡рджреЗрд╡рдВ рддреБ рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрдмрдиреНрддрдВ рддреБ ’ рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдЧрддрдГ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╡рд┐рдирд┐рдпреЛрдЧрдГ ред рдПрдХрд╛рджрд╢рд┐рдирд╕реНрдп рд╡реИрд╢реНрд╡рджреЗрд╡рд╕реНрдп рдкрд╢реЛрд░реНрд╡рдкрд╛рдпрд╛рдЧрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рдХреНрдпрд╛ тАШ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡реЗ рдЕрджреНрдп’ рдЗрддреНрдпреЗрд╖рд╛ ред рд╕реВрддреНрд░рд┐рддрдВ рдЪ — рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡реЗ рдЕрджреНрдп рдорд░реБрддреЛ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡ рдКрддреНрдпрд╛ рдиреЛ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдореБрдк рд╡реЗрддреБ рд╢рдВрд╕рдГ’ ( рдЖрд╢реНрд╡. рд╢реНрд░реМ. рей. рен) рдЗрддрд┐ рее

Jamison Brereton

35 (861)
All Gods
Lu┼Ыa Dh─Бn─Бka
14 verses: jagat─л, except triс╣гс╣нubh 13тАУ14
This is primarily a morning hymn, calling especially on the gods associated with the early morning sacrifice for aid and protection: the Sun, the Dawn, Agni, Indra, the A┼Ыvins, as well as Heaven and Earth. The ten interior verses (3тАУ12) have a p─Бda length refrain dedicated to the kindled ritual fire, and the activities of Dawn occupy much of the hymn (esp. vss. 3тАУ6). The hymn opens out toward its end, with special focus on the ─Аdityas (vss. 9, 11тАУ12), but the later prominence of the ─Аdityas has been prepared by mention of тАЬblamelessnessтАЭ in earlier verses (2тАУ3) and by the тАЬproclamation of truthтАЭ in verse 8. This truth, formulated in 8c, is simply that тАЬthe Sun, as spy,тАЭ rises every day, but we know from elsewhere in the R╠еgveda (nearby X.37 belonging to the same poetic group [see discussion there], as well as, e.g., VII.62.2, VII.63.1) that the Sun is the eye of the ─Аdityas, especially Mitra and Varuс╣Зa, who attests to the innocence or guilt of the men whom he sees as he rises. Thus this brief truth formulation encapsulates our knowledge that our place in the moral order is mediated through the cosmic order of the daily rhythm of sunrise.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe fires that are connected with Indra are awake, bringing light at the opening of the dawn; let thegreat heaven and earth be cognizant of that office; to-day we solicit the protection of the gods.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

At the opening ofthe dawn: when he dawn repels the darkness

Jamison Brereton

They have awakenedтАФthese fires accompanied by Indra, bringing light at the early brightenings of the dawn.
Let great Heaven and Earth take cognizance of our work. Today we
choose the help of the gods.

Griffith

THESE fires associate with Indra are awake, bringing their light when first the Dawn begins to shine.
May Heaven and Earth, great Pair, observe our holy work. We claim for us this day the favour of the Gods.

Geldner

Jetzt sind hier die Feuer, die den Indra zur Seite haben, erwacht, Licht bringend bei der Morgenr├╢te aufleuchten. Himmel und Erde, die gro├Яen sollen auf das Opferwerk achten. Wir erbitten uns heute der G├╢tter Gunst.

Grassmann

Schon sind erweckt die Feuer, welche Indra liebt, die Licht erregen bei des Morgens erstem Schein; Es m├╢gen Erd’ und Himmel achten auf das Werk; wir w├╝nschen heut der G├╢tter H├╝lfe uns herbei.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWe solicit the protection of heaven and earth; (we solicit) the maternal rivers, the mountains with theirlakes, the sun and the dawn, for freedom from sin; may the Soma that is now effused secure to us today goodfortune.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The mountains with their lakes = liс╣н, the mountains of (the lake) ┼Ъaryaс╣З─Бvat

Jamison Brereton

We choose the help of Heaven and Earth. The Mother Rivers, the Mountains filled with (soma-)reeds,
the Sun, the Dawn we beseech for blamelessness. Let Soma, being
pressed, make good for us today.

Griffith

Yea, for ourselves we claim the grace of Heaven and Earth, of Saryanavan, of the Hills and Mother Streams.
For innocence we pray to Surya and to Dawn. So may the flowing Soma bring us bliss to-day.

Geldner

Wir erbitten uns die Gunst von Himmel und Erde. Die m├╝tterlichen Fl├╝sse, die Berge von Saryanavat bitten wir um ihre Gunst. Surya, die Usas ersuchen wir um Schuldlosigkeit. Der ausgepre├Яte Soma soll uns heute Gl├╝ck schaffen.

Grassmann

Des Himmels und der Erde H├╝lfe flehn wir an, die Mutterstr├╢me und die somareichen H├╢hn, Um Unschuld flehn die Sonn’ und Morgenr├╢the wir; es schaff’ uns Heil der ausgepresste Soma heut,

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the vast maternal heaven and earth this day preserve us for our happiness, free from sin; may theopening dawn drive away our sin; we solicit the kindled fire for our welfare.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

May the opening dawn drive awayour sin: ucchanti = driving away the darkness– ucchant─л tam─Бс╣Гsi biv─Бsayant─л

Jamison Brereton

Heaven and EarthтАФlet the two great mothers protect us, who are blameless, for our welfare. Let Dawn, dawning, thrust away evil. тАУ We beseech Agni, when he is kindled, for well-being.

Griffith

May the great Twain, the Mothers, Heaven and Earth, this day preserve us free from sin for peace and happiness.
May Morning sending forth her light drive sin afar. We pray to kindled Agni for felicity.

Geldner

Himmel und Erde, die gro├Яen M├╝tter, sollen uns heute als Schuldlose beschirmen zur Wohlfahrt. Die aufleuchtende Morgenr├╢te soll das ├Ьbel vertreiben. - Um Heil bitten wir den entflammten Agni.

Grassmann

Als schuldlos m├╢gen heute Erd’ und Himmel uns, die reichen M├╝tter helfen uns zum Wohlergehn; Die Morgenr├╢the treibe leuchtend fort die Schuld, um Segen flehn wir den entflammten Agni an.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay this first dawn, the possessor of wealth, open; bringing to us who are liberal (a season) fit for thegods, abounding with riches; we consider the anger of the malevolent (to be) remote; we solicit the kindled firefor our welfare.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

We consideс╣Ы..remote: we put it far off

Jamison Brereton

This foremost ruddy one here, *this lovely goddessтАФlet her, the rich lady, dawn richly for our gain.
In the distance (from us) we would set the fury of the one who is bad to meet. тАУ We beseech Agni, when he is kindled, for well-being.

Griffith

May this first Dawn bring us the host of gracious Gods: rich, may it richly shine for us who strive for wealth.
The wrath of the malignant may we keep afar. We pray to kindled Agni for feilicity.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬDawns, who are associated with the rays of the sun, bringing light at the opening (of the day), shineupon us today, propitious, for our subsistence; we solicit the kindled fire for our welfare.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Those who stretch forth with the rays of the sun, bringing light at the early brightenings of the dawn,
do you dawn good things widely today for our fame. тАУ We beseech
Agni, when he is kindled, for well-being.

Griffith

Dawns, who come forward with the bright beams of the Sun, and at your earliest flushing bring to us the light,
Shine ye on us to-day auspicious, for renown. We pray to kindled Agni for felicity.

Geldner

Grassmann

Ihr, die ihr mit der Sonne Strahlen vorw├дrtsdringt, das Licht erweckend bei des Morgens erstem Schein, Erstrahlet heute gl├дnzend uns zu hohem Ruhm; um Segen flehn wir den entflammten Agni an.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬMay the salutary dawns hasten to us; may the fires blaze up with great lustre, and may the A┼Ыvinsharness their quick-going chariot; we solicit the kindled fire for our welfare.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Let the dawns without affliction attend upon us; let the fires rear up loftily with their light.
Let the A┼Ыvins hitch up their thrusting chariot. тАУ We beseech Agni,
when he is kindled, for well-being.

Griffith

Free from all sickness may the Mornings come to us, and let our fires mount upward with a lofty blaze.
The Asvin Pair have harnessed their swift-moving car. We pray to kindled Agni for felicity.

Geldner

Ohne Krankheit sollen uns die Usas kommen, hoch sollen mit ihrer Helle die Feuer emporschlagen. Die Asvin haben ihren eiligen Wagen geschirrt. - Um Heil bitten wir den entflammten Agni.

Grassmann

Die Morgen m├╢gen zu uns kommen ohne Leid, die Feuer hell erheben sich mit ihrem Licht, Den raschen Wagen schirrten schon die Ritter sich; um Segen flehn wir den entflammten Agni an.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬSavit─Б, this day bestow upon us excellent and eligible portion, for you verily are the dispenser ofwealth; I recite the praise (of the gods) which is the progenitress of riches; we solicit the kindled fire for ourwelfare.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The best portion, worthy to be chosen, impel to us today, o Savitar, for you are a conferrer of treasure.
I call on her, the begetter of wealth, on the Holy Place. тАУ We beseech Agni, when he is kindled, for well-being.

Griffith

Send us to-day a portion choice and excellent, O Savitar, for thou art he who dealeth wealth.
I cry to Dhisana, Mother of opulence. We pray to kindled Agni for felicity.

Geldner

Grassmann

English translation:

тАЬMay that glorification of the gods which men repeat in connection with the rite preserve me; the sunrises visiting all the lustre of the dawn; we solicit the kindled fire for our welfare.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Let this proclamation of truth carry me through, the one that as sons of Manu we have thought up for the gods:
тАЬThrough all the ruddy (dawns) the Sun, as spy, (always) goes up.тАЭ
тАУ We beseech Agni, when he is kindled, for well-being.

Further me this declaring of Eternal Law, the Law of Gods, as we mortals acknowledge it!
The Sun goes up beholding all the rays of morn. We pray to kindled Agni for felicity.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬOn strewing the sacred grass, and bringing the stones into contact (with the Soma), whereby ourwishes are accomplished, we solicit today the benevolent (─Аdityas); abiding in the happiness of those ─Аdityas,you discharged, worshipper, your duties, we solicit the kindled fire for our welfare.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Whereby our wishes areaccomplished: manmanas s─Бdhe = liс╣н, on the accomplishment of our wishes; or, an epithet of yoga, the bringinginto contact, which is the accomplisher (s─Бdhake) of our wishes; you discharge your duties: bhuraс╣Зyasi =kartavy─Бni karm─Бс╣Зi bibharс╣гi, you practise the acts that are to be performed

Jamison Brereton

Today at the strewing of the ritual grass, at the yoking of the pressing stones we beg for lack of hatred and for the realization of our
thought.
Standing in the shelter of the ─Аdityas, you are astir. тАУ We beseech Agni, when he is kindled, for well-being.

Griffith

This day we pray with innocence in strewing grass, adjusting pressing-stones, and perfecting the hymn.
Thou in the Adityas’ keeping movest restlessly. We pray to kindled Agni for felicity.

Geldner

Wir bitten heute um Friedfertigkeit bei des Barhis Auslegen und bei der Pre├Яsteine T├дtigkeit, da├Я unsere Andacht erfolgreich sei. Im Schutze der Aditya┬┤s stehend bist du t├дtig. - Um Heil bitten wir den entflammten Agni.

Grassmann

Wir flehen arglos bei der Streubereitung heut, beim Schirr’n der Steine und bei des Gebetes Werk; In der Aditja’s Schutze stehend regst du dich; um Segen flehn wir den entflammten Agni an.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬOn this our sacred grass, spacious and bright where the gods delight together, do you (Agni) seat theseven ministrant priests, Indra, Mitra, Varuс╣Зa, Bhaga, I praise the gods for their bounty; we solicit the kindled firefor our welfare.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

I praise the gods for their bounty: dev─Бn ─лс╕╖e, s─Бtaye

Jamison Brereton

Here is our ritual grass for the joint revelry. I reverently invoke the gods lofty in heaven. I will make the seven Hotars sit (on the ritual grass).
(We beseech) Indra, Mitra, Varuс╣Зa, and Bhaga, for our gain. тАУ We
beseech Agni, when he is kindled, for well-being.

Griffith

To our great holy grass I bid the Gods at morn to banquet, and will seat them as the seven priests,-
Varuna, Indra, Mitra, Bhaga for our gain. We pray to kindled Agni for felicity.

Geldner

Auf unser hohes Barhis rufe ich zu gemeinsamem Gelage die G├╢tter im Himmel her, hei├Яe ich die sieben Hotri Platz nehmen. Den Indra, Mitra, Varuna, Bhaga, um das Gl├╝ck zu gewinnen, - Um Heil bitten wir den entflammten Agni.

Grassmann

Die sieben Priester setz’ ich nun auf unsre Streu beim Mahl, und r├╝hm’ die G├╢tter in dem Himmel laut, Den Indra, Bhaga, Mitra Varuna zum Heil; um Segen flehn wir den entflammten Agni an.

English translation:

тАЬThis day, may all the Maruts, all the (deities), be for our protection; and may all the fires be kindleс╕НMay all the gods come for our preservation, and may all wealth and food be ours.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Protection: ┼лt─л, avas─Б =rakс╣гaс╣Зam;

Alternative: ┼лt─л = tarpaс╣Зam, satisfaction;

Avas─Б = tuс╣гс╣нi, plural asure

Jamison Brereton

Let all the Maruts today all (be there) with aid, let all the kindled fires be (there with aid).
Let all the gods come here to us with help; let all wealth, (every) prize be for us.1434 X.36

Griffith

This day may all the Maruts, all he near us with aid: may all our fires be well enkindled.
May all Gods come to us with gracious favour. May spoil and wealth he ours, and all possessions.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬGods, who are prompt (to grant our desires), may he, whom you guard in battle, whom you defend(from his enemies), whom having extricated from sin, you gratify (in all his wishes), who (secure) in yourprotection; knows not of fear, may we (who are all this) be assiduous in offering sacrifice to the gods.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

One whom you help, o gods, at the winning of prizes, one whom you safeguard, one whom you carry across narrow straits,
one who knows no fear under your protectionтАФmay we be (all) those, to pursue the gods, powerful ones.

Griffith

He whom ye aid, O Deities, in battle, whom ye protect and rescue from affliction,
Who fears no danger at your milk-libation, -such may we be to feast the Gods, ye Mighty.

Geldner

Grassmann

Wem ihr, o G├╢tter, h├╝lfreich seid in der Schlacht, wen ihr besch├╝tzt und durch Drangsal hindurchf├╝hrt; wer von euch beh├╝tet wird, der kennt [veda tonlos zu lesen] keine Gefahr; solche m├╢gen auch wir sein zur G├╢tterbewirthung, o ihr starken.

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рджреЗрд╡рд╛рд╕рдГ-рдпрдВ рд╡рд╛рдЬрд╕рд╛рддреМ-рдЕрд╡рде) рд╣реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдВрд╕рдГ ! рдпрдВ рдЬрдирдВ рдЦрд▓реНрд╡рдореГрддрд╛рдиреНрдирднреЛрдЧрдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддреМ рдореБрдХреНрддрд┐рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддреМ рд░рдХреНрд╖рде рд╕рдореНрдкрд╛рджрдпрдд тАЬрдЕрдореГрддреЛрд╜рдиреНрдирдВ рд╡реИ рд╡рд╛рдЬрдГтАЭ [рдЬреИрежрезредрезрепрей] (рдпрдВ рддреНрд░рд╛рдпрдзреНрд╡реЗ) рдпрдордзрд┐рдХрд╛рд░рд┐рдгрдВ рднрдпрд╛рддреН рддреНрд░рд╛рдпрдзреНрд╡реЗ рдкреГрдердХреН рдХреБрд░реБрде (рдпрдореН-рдЕрдВрд╣рдГ рдЕрддрд┐ рдкрд┐рдкреГрде) рдпрдВ рдкрд╛рдкрдорддрд┐рдХреНрд░рд╛рдореНрдп рдкрд╛рд▓рдпрдд (рдпрдГ рд╡рдГ-рдЧреЛрдкреАрдереЗ рднрдпрд╕реНрдп рди рд╡реЗрдж) рдпрдГ рдЦрд▓реБ рдпреБрд╖реНрдорд╛рдХрдВ рд╡рд╛рдХреНрдкрд╛рдиреЗ рд╡реЗрджрд╛рдзреНрдпрдпрдиреЗ рд╡реЗрджрд╛рдзреНрдпрдпрдирд╛рдп рдХрд┐рдордкрд┐ рднрдпрдВ рди рд╡реЗрддреНрддрд┐, рддрдерд╛рднреВрддрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╡рд┐рджреБрд╖рд╛рдВ рд╕рдВрд░рдХреНрд╖рдгреЗ (рджреЗрд╡рд╡реАрддрдпреЗ) рджрд┐рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рднреЛрдЧрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╡реАрддрд┐рдГ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрд┐рд░реНрдпрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдВ рддрд╕реНрдпреИ рдореБрдХреНрддреНрдпреИ тАЬрджреЗрд╡рд╡реАрддрдпреЗ рджрд┐рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдирд╛рдВ тАжтАж рднреЛрдЧрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрд┐рдГтАЭ [рдпрдЬреБреж релредреп рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрджрдГ] (рддреЗ рддреБрд░рд╛рд╕рдГ рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдо) рддреЗ рд╡рдпрдВ рд╕рдВрд╕рд╛рд░рд╕рд╛рдЧрд░рдВ рддрд░рдиреНрддрдГ-рддреАрд░реНрдгрд╛рдГ тАЬрддреБрд░рдГ-рддрд░рддреЗрд░реНрд╡рд╛тАЭ [рдирд┐рд░реБреж резреиредрезрек] рднрд╡реЗрдо реерезрекрее
